Utah Code Annotated - Title 63B - Bonds
=======================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63B - Chapter 1 - General Provisions
****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(1): "Bond anticipation note" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(1)(a): any financing note issued according to the procedures and requirements of this title in anticipation of the receipt of the proceeds of the sale of the bonds authorized under this title; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(1)(b): any renewal of those notes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(2): "Bonds" means any bonds, bond anticipation notes, or other obligations authorized under this title for which the full faith, credit, and resources and ad valorem taxing power of the state have been pledged for the payment of the principal of and interest on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(3): "Capital project" means any land, building, facility, highway, improvement, equipment, or other property, or combination of them, that the state of Utah or any of its agencies, divisions, institutions, or other administrative subunits are authorized by law to acquire or construct.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(4): 63B-1-201 "Commission" means the State Bonding Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(5): "Division" means the Division of Facilities Construction and Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-101(6): "Sinking fund" means the fund or account established as provided in this title to hold money to pay the principal and interest on each series of bonds as they become due.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201 Members -- Powers and duties -- Per diem.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(1): There is created a State Bonding Commission composed of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(1)(a): the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(1)(b): the state treasurer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(1)(c): a third person appointed by the governor to serve a four-year term, who is a member of a political party different from that of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(1)(d): When the at-large position becomes vacant for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(2): The commission shall exercise the powers and perform the duties prescribed for the commission by statute.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(3): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(3)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(3)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-201(3)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-202 Bond legislation to contain operation cost estimates of funded projects.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-202(1): As used in this section, "capital projects" means buildings but does not include highways, roads, or capital improvements to buildings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-202(2): All legislation authorizing the commission to issue bonds for the acquisition and construction of capital projects shall contain an estimate of the annual amount of funds necessary to operate and maintain each capital project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-202(3): If any operations and maintenance costs estimates required by this section are omitted from any legislation authorizing the commission to issue bonds, that omission does not affect the authority of the commission to issue bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-301 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part shall be known as the "State Building Ownership Authority Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302 Legislative findings.
-----------------------------------------------------
The Legislature finds and declares as follows:Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302(1): it is the policy of this state to provide office space and related facilities for state bodies and such other governmental facilities and property, including highways and highway rights-of-way, as may be necessary or desirable, in the most efficient and economical way possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302(2): many state bodies are inadequately provided with necessary office space, related facilities, other governmental facilities, and property to serve the public welfare;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302(3): the state is renting space for state bodies in privately owned buildings with funds which could more efficiently and economically be put to use toward the purchase and acquisition of  facilities by the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302(4): in order to provide for a fully adequate supply of office space, related facilities, other governmental facilities, and property at the lowest possible cost, this Legislature should establish a State Building Ownership Authority for the purpose of financing, owning, leasing, operating, or encumbering such facilities to meet the needs of the state government and to serve the public welfare;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302(5): the foregoing involve public purposes and uses for which public money may be borrowed, expended, advanced, loaned, or granted, the activities specified would serve a public purpose in improving or otherwise benefiting the people of this state and, therefore, this part is in the public interest and is declared to be in the public interest as a matter of express legislative determination; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-302(6): the compelling need within this state for the creation of an adequate supply of office space, related facilities, other government facilities, and property for state bodies at a low cost can be best met by the establishment of a body corporate and politic vested with the powers and duties specified in this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(1): "Acquire or construct," "acquired or constructed," "constructed or acquired," "acquiring or constructing," or "acquisition or construction" means any acquisition, construction, reconstruction, restoration, enlargement, improvement, renovation, repair, replacement, equipping or furnishing, in whole or in part, of a facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(2): "Authority" means the State Building Ownership Authority created by this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(3): "Division" means the Division of Facilities Construction and Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(4)(a): "Facility" or "facilities" means any public building, structure, highway, or property for any governmental purpose of state bodies, and the related and appurtenant easements, rights-of-way, improvements, paving, utilities, landscaping, parking facilities, and the lands, interests in land, and grounds, together with the personal property necessary, convenient, or appurtenant to them.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(4)(b): "Facility" includes a golf course.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(5): "Mortgage" means any mortgage, trust deed, indenture, pledge agreement, assignment, security agreement, financing statement, or other instrument that encumbers property as security for obligations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(6)(a): "Obligations" means any mortgage certificates, notes, debentures, interim certificates, revenue bonds, or other evidences of financial indebtedness.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(6)(b): "Obligations" does not mean general obligation bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(7): (7)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(7)(a): "State body" or "state bodies" means the state and any department, board, commission, or agency of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(7)(b): (7)(c) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-303(7)(c): "State body" or "state bodies" includes a college or university when the obligation to be issued will finance the acquisition or construction of research facilities, housing facilities, or student centers at the college or university.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304 State Building Ownership Authority created -- Members -- Compensation -- Location in Department of Administrative Services.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(1): There is created a body politic and corporate to be known as the State Building Ownership Authority composed of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(1)(a): the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(1)(b): the state treasurer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(1)(c): the executive director of the Department of Government Operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(2): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(2)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(2)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(2)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(3): 67-4-16
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(3)(a): Upon request, the division shall provide staff support to the State Building Ownership Authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-304(3)(b): 67-4-16 The State Building Ownership Authority may seek and obtain independent financial advice, support, and information from the state financial advisor created under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305 Powers and duties of authority.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(1): The authority shall have perpetual succession as a body politic and corporate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2): The authority may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(a): sue and to be sued in its own name;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(b): have, and alter at will, an official seal;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(c): contract with experts, advisers, consultants, and agents for needed services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(d): with the prior approval of the Legislature, borrow money and issue obligations, including refunding obligations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(e): receive and accept aid or contributions from any source, including the United States or this state, in the form of money, property, labor, or other things of value to be held, used and applied to carry out the purposes of this part, subject to the conditions upon which this aid and contributions are made, for any purpose consistent with this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(f): enter into agreements with any department, agency or instrumentality of the United States or this state, financial institutions, or contractors for the purpose of leasing, maintaining, and operating any facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(g): to the extent permitted under its contract with the holders of its obligations, consent to any modification relating to rate of interest, time and payment of any installment of principal or interest, security or any other term of any contract, mortgage, mortgage loan, mortgage loan commitment, contract or agreement of any kind to which it is a party;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(h): pledge revenues from any facility to secure the payment of obligations relating to that facility, including interest on obligations, and to redeem those obligations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(i): cause to be executed mortgages, trust deeds, indentures, pledge agreements, assignments, security agreements, and financing statements encumbering property acquired, or constructed under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(j): own, lease, operate, and encumber facilities acquired or constructed under this chapter by it or the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(k): exercise the power of eminent domain;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(l): rent or lease any facility in whole or in part to any state body; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(2)(m): have and exercise any other powers or duties that are necessary or appropriate to carry out and effectuate the purposes of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(3): 63C-25-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(3)(a): 63C-25-201 The authority shall submit an annual written report of the authority's proceedings to the State Finance Review Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(3)(b): The report shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(3)(b)(i): a description of any outstanding money borrowed and obligations issued by the authority, including loan amounts, terms, and security;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(3)(b)(ii): facilities funded by the actions of the authority; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-305(3)(b)(iii): an explanation of why the financing terms and obligations used for a facility are appropriate and in the best interest of the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306 Obligations issued by authority -- Limitation of liability on obligations -- Limitation on amount of obligations issued.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(1)(a): All obligations issued by the authority under this part shall be limited obligations of the authority and may not constitute, nor give rise to, a general obligation or liability of, nor a charge against the general credit or taxing power of, this state or any of its political subdivisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(1)(b): This limitation shall be plainly stated upon all obligations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2): (2); Title 63B, Chapter 6, Part 2, 1997 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 6, Part 3, 1997 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 7, Part 2, 1998 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 7, Part 3, 1998 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 8, Part 2, 1999 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 8, Part 3, 1999 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 10, Part 1, 2001 Highway General Obligation Bonds; Title 63B, Chapter 10, Part 2, 2001 Highway General Obligation Bond Anticipation Notes Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 11, Part 5, 2002 Highway General Obligation Bonds for Salt Lake County; Title 63B, Chapter 11, Part 6, 2002 Highway General Obligation Bond Anticipation Notes for Salt Lake County; 63B-13-102; 63B-16-101; 63B-16-102; 63B-18-401; 63B-18-402; Title 63B, Chapter 27, Part 1, 2017 Highway General Obligation Bonds; 63B-7-503; (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2)(a): No authority obligations incurred under this section may be issued in an amount exceeding the difference between the total indebtedness of the state and an amount equal to 1-1/2% of the value of the taxable property of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2)(b): (2); Title 63B, Chapter 6, Part 2, 1997 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 6, Part 3, 1997 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 7, Part 2, 1998 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 7, Part 3, 1998 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 8, Part 2, 1999 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 8, Part 3, 1999 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 10, Part 1, 2001 Highway General Obligation Bonds; Title 63B, Chapter 10, Part 2, 2001 Highway General Obligation Bond Anticipation Notes Authorization; Title 63B, Chapter 11, Part 5, 2002 Highway General Obligation Bonds for Salt Lake County; Title 63B, Chapter 11, Part 6, 2002 Highway General Obligation Bond Anticipation Notes for Salt Lake County; 63B-13-102; 63B-16-101; 63B-16-102; 63B-18-401; 63B-18-402; Title 63B, Chapter 27, Part 1, 2017 Highway General Obligation Bonds Debt issued under authority of the following parts or sections may not be included as part of the total indebtedness of the state of Utah in determining the debt limit established by this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2)(b)(i): Title 63B, Chapter 6, Part 2, 1997 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2)(b)(ii): Title 63B, Chapter 6, Part 3, 1997 Highway Bond Anticipation Note Authorization
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2)(b)(iii): Title 63B, Chapter 7, Part 2, 1998 Highway General Obligation Bond Authorization

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(2)(c): 63B-7-503; (2) Debt issued under authority of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3): The obligations shall be authorized by resolution of the authority, following approval of the Legislature, and may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(a): be executed and delivered at any time, and from time to time, as the authority may determine;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(b): be sold at public or private sale in the manner and at the prices, either at, in excess of, or below their face value and at the times that the authority determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(c): be in the form and denominations that the authority determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(d): be of the tenor that the authority determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(e): be in registered or bearer form either as to principal or interest or both;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(f): be payable in those installments and at the times that the authority determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(g): be payable at the places, either within or without this state, that the authority determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(h): bear interest at the rate or rates, payable at the place or places, and evidenced in the manner, that the authority determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(i): be redeemable before maturity, with or without premium;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(j): contain any other provisions not inconsistent with this part that are considered to be for the best interests of the authority and provided for in the proceedings of the authority under which the bonds are authorized to be issued; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(3)(k): bear facsimile signatures and seals.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-306(4): The authority may pay any expenses, premiums, or commissions, that it considers necessary or advantageous in connection with the authorization, sale, and issuance of these obligations, from the proceeds of the sale of the obligations or from the revenues of the projects involved.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307 Lease of facilities to state bodies -- Rental.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(1): The authority and state bodies shall enter into leases or agreements for the use and occupancy of any portion of any facility constructed or acquired under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(2): The leases or agreements may provide for the operation, maintenance, and insurance of the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3): The leases and agreements shall provide that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(a): the rental to be paid annually by each state body to the authority for the use and occupancy is in proportion to the space occupied in the facility by that state body;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(b): those rentals shall be in an amount sufficient to completely pay all principal and interest on those obligations as they come due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(c): those rentals may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(c)(i): the cost of maintenance, operation, and insurance of those facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(c)(ii): the expenses of the authority in administering the facilities under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(c)(iii): amounts needed to provide reserves to secure obligations, to maintain, repair, renovate, reconstruct, or replace those facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-307(3)(c)(iv): any other reserves and funds that the authority considers necessary or advisable in order to sell its obligations.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308 Payment of obligations out of rentals -- Other governmental entities not liable for payment -- Appropriations for increased rentals -- Defaulting bodies to quit premises.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(1): Except as secured as provided in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(1)(a): each obligation issued or caused to be issued by the authority, and the interest on that obligation, is payable solely out of rentals or lease payments received by the authority for the facilities constructed or acquired under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(1)(b): each obligation shall state that information on its face.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(2): Except to the extent that facilities are encumbered, nothing in this part may be construed to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(2)(a): require the state, or any department, board, commission, agency, or political subdivision of the state, other than the authority, to pay any part of any obligation issued or caused to be issued under this part, or any interest on any of those obligations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(2)(b): require the state or any department, board, commission, agency or political subdivision of the state, other than the state body or state bodies leasing any portion of the facilities, to pay any rental due to the authority by any state body under the terms of any lease of facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(2)(c): require the Legislature to appropriate any money to pay these obligations, interest, or rentals.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(3): If the rentals paid by a state body to the authority are insufficient to pay the principal and interest on the obligations or other amounts payable from rentals when due, the governor may request the Legislature to appropriate additional funds to that body for the payment of increased rentals.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-308(4): If a state body fails to pay any rentals due to the authority under the terms of any lease or agreement for facilities, that body shall immediately quit and vacate the portion of that facility that it has occupied under that lease or agreement, and the rental or lease obligation under the lease or agreement shall then cease.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309 Securing of obligations -- Provisions in mortgages given as security -- Procedure upon default.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(1): The principal and interest on any obligation issued under this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(1)(a): shall be secured by a pledge and assignment of the revenues out of which that obligation shall be made payable;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(1)(b): may be secured by a mortgage covering all or any part of the facility for which the revenues from the obligation were used;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(1)(c): may be secured by a pledge and assignment of the lease of that facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(1)(d): may be secured by any other security device on that facility that is considered most advantageous by the authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(a): The proceedings under which the obligations are authorized to be issued under this part and any mortgage given to secure the obligations may contain any agreements and provisions customarily contained in instruments securing obligations, including, but not limited to, provisions respecting:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(a)(i): the fixing and collection of rents for any facility covered by the proceedings or mortgage;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(a)(ii): the terms to be incorporated in the lease of that facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(a)(iii): the operation, maintenance, and insurance of that facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(a)(iv): the creation and maintenance of special reserve or other funds and accounts from the proceeds of sale of obligations or from the revenues of that facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(a)(v): the rights and remedies available in the event of a default to the holders of obligations or to the trustee under a mortgage, as the authority may determine in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(2)(b): All these mortgages, trust deeds, security agreements, or trust indentures shall provide that no deficiency judgment upon foreclosure may be entered against the authority, this state, or any of its political subdivisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(3): The proceedings authorizing obligations under this part, and any mortgage securing these obligations, may provide that, if there is a default in the payment of the principal of or the interest on these obligations or in the performance of any agreement contained in the proceedings or mortgage, the payment or performance may be enforced by the appointment of a receiver relative to that facility with power to charge and collect rents and to apply the revenues from the facility in accordance with the proceedings or the provisions of the mortgage.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(4)(a): Any mortgage made under this part to secure obligations issued pursuant to it may also provide that, in the event of a default in the payment of the mortgage or the violation of any agreement contained in the mortgage, the mortgage may be foreclosed or otherwise realized on in any manner permitted by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(4)(b): The mortgage may also provide that any trustee under the mortgage or the holder of any of the obligations secured by the mortgage may become the purchaser at any foreclosure sale, if that trustee is highest bidder.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-309(4)(c): A breach of the agreement does not impose any general obligation or liability upon, nor a charge against, the authority or the general credit or taxing power of this state or any of its political subdivisions.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-310 Proceeds from sale of obligations -- Use.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-310(1): The proceeds from the sale of obligations issued under this part may be applied only for the purposes for which the obligations were issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-310(2): Any accrued interest and premium received upon the sale, and any portion of the proceeds that may not be needed for the purposes for which the obligations were issued, shall be applied to the payment of the principal of, or the interest on, the obligations.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311 Cost of acquiring or constructing facility.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
The cost of acquiring or constructing any facility shall be considered to include the following:Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(1): the actual cost of acquiring or improving real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(2): the actual cost of enlarging, constructing, reconstructing, improving, replacing, restoring, renovating, maintaining, equipping, or furnishing all or any part of a facility, including architects' or engineers' fees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(3): all expenses connected with the authorization, sale, and issuance of the obligations to finance the acquisition or construction, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(3)(a): fees for outside attorneys or accountants whose opinions are required to secure the issuance of those obligations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(3)(b): financial advisors' fees and commissions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(3)(c): printing costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(3)(d): those amounts that the authority considers necessary to establish bond reserves and maintenance, repair, replacement, and contingency funds and accounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-311(3)(e): the interest on these obligations for a reasonable time before, during, and for a reasonable period of time after, completion of the acquisition or construction.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-312 Signature of former member or officer of authority -- Continuing validity.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If any of the members or officers of the authority no longer occupy their position at the time of the delivery of any obligations signed by them, their signatures or facsimiles of their signatures are valid and sufficient for all purposes, as if they had remained in office until that delivery.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-313 Negotiability of obligations -- Registration.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
All obligations of the authority are negotiable instruments within the meaning of, and for all purposes of

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-314 Person executing obligations not personally liable.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No person executing any obligations issued under this part is subject to personal liability or accountability because of the issuance.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-315 Tax exemption.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-315(1): All property acquired or held by the authority under this part is declared to be public property used for essential public and governmental purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-315(2): All property and income from it, and all obligations issued under this part, the interest payable on them, and income derived from them, are exempt from all taxation imposed by this state or any of its political subdivisions, except for the corporate franchise tax.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-316 Obligations as legal investments -- Deposit of obligations.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-316(1): The obligations issued under this part are securities in which all persons and organizations authorized to invest in any obligations of this state may properly and legally invest any funds, including capital belonging to them or within their control.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-316(2): These obligations are also declared to be securities that may properly and legally be deposited with, and received by, any state, county, or municipal officer, or agency of the state for any purpose for which the deposit of any obligations of the state is authorized by law.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1-321(2): all these obligations, agreements, and security are declared to constitute legally binding obligations of the authority and all state bodies relating to them in accordance with their terms.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 63B - Chapter 1a - Master General Obligation Bond Act
*********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101 Definitions -- Bonds authorized -- Prohibitions -- Purposes -- Maturity -- Use of bonds proceeds.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1)(a): "Cost" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1)(a)(i): all costs related to the authorized capital project, including the cost of equipment and furnishings for, interests in, or improvements necessary, incidental, or convenient to, those capital projects;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1)(a)(ii): all costs incident to the authorization and issuance of bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1)(a)(iii): interest estimated to accrue on bonds during the period to be covered by the acquisition and construction of the capital project and for up to 12 months after that period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1)(a)(iv): other amounts that the commission finds necessary to establish reserve funds and to provide working capital related to the capital project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(1)(b): "Taxable property of the state" includes all real and personal property subject to ad valorem taxation within the state, including all property subject to a fee-in lieu of tax.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(2): When authorized by the Legislature, the commission may, in the manner specified in this chapter, issue bonds to provide funds to the state for the purpose of paying all or part of the cost of designing, acquiring, constructing, improving, or extending:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(2)(a): any one or more capital projects; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(2)(b): any interest in one or more or any combination of capital projects.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(3): Before issuing any bonds, the commission shall determine that the Legislature has:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(3)(a): affirmatively authorized the issuance of the bonds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(3)(b): has specified:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(3)(b)(i): for capital projects, the capital projects to be funded; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(3)(b)(ii): the maximum amount of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(4): The commission shall either:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(4)(a): comply with any maturity requirements established by the Legislature; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(4)(b): in the absence of any maturity requirements, establish, by resolution, a bond maturity date or dates that are not later than 15 years after the date of delivery of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(5)(a): The commission may not issue bonds under this chapter in an amount that violates the limitation described in the
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-101(5)(b): For purposes of applying the debt limitation contained in the Utah Constitution Article XIV, Section 1, the value of the taxable property in Utah is considered to be 100% of the fair market value of the taxable property of the state as computed from the last assessment for state purposes made before the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102 Commission responsibilities -- Manner of issuance -- Plan of financing -- Registration -- Signatures -- Replacement -- Reporting.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1): The commission may determine by resolution:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(a): the manner in which bonds issued under this chapter may be authorized, sold, and issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(b): to issue bonds in one or more series;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(c): the amounts, dates, interest rates, including a variable rate or rates, and maturity dates of the bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(d): the manner of sale, including public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(e): the terms and conditions of sale, including price, whether at, below, or above face value;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(f): the denominations, registration, exchange, form, including book-entry only, manner of execution, manner of authentication, place and medium of purchase, redemption terms, and tender rights of the bonds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(1)(g): other provisions and details that it considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(2): The commission may, by resolution, adopt a plan of financing, which may include terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the commission on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for bond insurance, letters of credit, standby bond purchase agreements, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements relating to the bonds, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(3): The commission may provide for the services and payment for the services of one or more financial institutions or other entities, persons, or nominees, within or outside the state, for the authentication, registration, transfer, including record, bookkeeping, or book-entry functions, exchange, and payment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(4): The commission may provide for the calculation and payment to the United States of whatever amounts are necessary to comply with the Internal Revenue Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(5)(a): The commission shall, by resolution, authorize a public official to sign the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(5)(b): That signature may be a facsimile signature of that official that is imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(5)(c): If all signatures of public officials on the bonds are facsimile signatures, the commission shall provide for a manual authenticating signature on the bonds by or on behalf of a designated authentication agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(5)(d): If a public official ceases to hold office before delivery of the bonds signed by that official, the signature or facsimile signature of the public official is nevertheless valid for all purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(6): The commission may cause a facsimile of the state seal to be imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(7): The commission shall provide an annual report of its proceedings to the governor to include in his budget for as long as any bonds issued under this chapter remain outstanding.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(8): 63C-25-201

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(8)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(8)(b)(i): The report shall include a description of any outstanding bonds issued by the authority, including loan amounts, terms, and security; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-102(8)(b)(ii): an explanation of why the loan amounts and terms are appropriate for the project and in the best interest of the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201 Bonds proceeds -- Deposits -- Investment -- Disposition of investment income and unexpended proceeds.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(1)(a): The commission shall provide that proceeds from the sale of bonds issued under this chapter are deposited within one or more accounts as determined by the commission or by the state treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(1)(b): The state treasurer shall administer and maintain these accounts.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(2)(a): The state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(2)(a)(i): establish the kinds of investments in which the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter may be invested; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(2)(a)(ii): designate where the income from the investment of bond proceeds shall be applied.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(2)(b): The state treasurer shall apply the income from the investment of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter as directed by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-201(3): Upon completion of the purposes for which the bonds were issued, any unexpended proceeds of the bonds issued under this chapter shall be deposited in the related sinking fund unless the commission provides otherwise by resolution.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301 Sinking fund -- Creation -- Investment of money.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(1): For bonds authorized and issued as provided in this chapter, the commission shall create a sinking fund, to be administered by the state treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(2): All money deposited in the sinking fund, from whatever source, shall be used to pay debt service on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(3): The commission or the state treasurer may create separate accounts within the sinking fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(4): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(4)(a): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(4)(b): Unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter, the treasurer:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(4)(b)(i): shall deposit all income from the investment of any sinking fund money into the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-301(4)(b)(ii): may use it for the payment of debt service on the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-302 Payment of interest, principal, and redemption premiums.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-302(1): The Division of Finance shall draw warrants on the state treasury before any interest, principal, or redemption premiums become due on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-302(2): After receipt of the warrants, the state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-302(2)(a): promptly pay the warrants from funds within the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-302(2)(b): immediately transmit the amount paid to the paying agent for the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-303 Tax levy -- Abatement of tax.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-303(1): Each year after issuance of bonds and until each outstanding bond is retired, there is levied a direct annual tax on all taxable property of the state sufficient to pay principal, interest, and any applicable redemption premiums on each bond as it becomes due.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-303(2): The State Tax Commission shall fix the rate of the direct annual tax levy each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-303(3): The tax shall be collected and the proceeds applied as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-303(4): 63B-1a-301 The proceeds of all taxes levied under this section are appropriated to the sinking fund established as required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-303(5): The direct annual tax imposed under this section is abated to the extent that money is available from sources other than ad valorem taxes in the sinking fund for the payment of bond interest, principal, and redemption premiums.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-402 Legal investment status.
---------------------------------------------------------
Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments for all state trust funds, insurance companies, banks, trust companies, and the State School Fund and may be used as collateral to secure legal obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1a-403 Tax status -- Exemption.
---------------------------------------------------------
The bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the bonds, and any income from the bonds is not taxable in Utah for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-101 Title.

This chapter is known as the "State Financing Consolidation Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-102 Definitions.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-102(3): "Authorizing agency" means the board, person, or unit with legal responsibility for administering and managing revolving loan funds.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-102(4)(b): an indenture or other similar document authorized by the commission that authorizes and secures outstanding revenue bonds from time to time.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-102(5): 63B-1-201 "Commission" means the State Bonding Commission, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-102(6): "Revenue bonds" means any special fund revenue bonds issued under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-103 Limitation on issuance of bonds -- Legislative approval required.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No bonds may be authorized or issued under this chapter without the prior approval of the Legislature.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201 Investment officer -- Powers and duties.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(1): There is created within the Office of the State Treasurer an investment banking officer to advise, counsel, and render technical assistance to authorizing agencies in the management of state loan and grant programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(2): This officer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(2)(a): work cooperatively with the staff and boards of authorizing agencies as an advisor on technical financial aspects concerning loan and grant programs authorized by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(2)(b): coordinate procedures for the closing of and assist authorizing agencies in closing all loans and grants of funds or other subsidy agreements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(2)(c): analyze, in conjunction with the appropriate authorizing agency, the financial feasibility and economic and capital efficiency of projects of applicants to authorizing agencies for loans and grants, review financing options, and make recommendations to each authorizing agency regarding terms of loans or grants and levels of state subsidy in accordance with the financial feasibility of the project and the efficiency of available state capital;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(2)(d): coordinate and consolidate, to the extent possible, all financial and legal analysis of financing plans and closings of loans and grants made by each authorizing agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(2)(e): provide an annual report of the officer's activities to the state treasurer, the governor, the Division of Finance, and the boards of each authorizing agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3): (2)(c) The analysis under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3)(a): a demonstration of need based on the applicant's overall financial profile, including overlapping debt, tax levies, user rates, fees, charges, assessments, and other revenue and obligations existing within the community as a whole;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3)(b): the ability of the applicant to obtain financing from other, preferably private, sources on terms and conditions reasonably affordable;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3)(c): the availability and advisability of financing methods such as loans, grants, interest buy down arrangements, bond insurance, loan or bond guarantees, or any other appropriate method;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3)(d): the economic and efficiency of capital advantages enuring to the authorizing agency if the financing plan is adopted;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3)(e): a demonstration of local public support for the financing plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(3)(f): availability of other funds and financing methods under law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-201(4): Each authorizing agency shall consult with and cooperate with the officer and shall consider the officer's recommendations before proceeding to fund a project, but the final decision as to the appropriate financing plan shall rest with the board of the authorizing agency according to their legal authority existing at the time.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-402(4)(e): Revenue bonds do not constitute debt of the state within the meaning of Utah Constitution Article XIII, Sec. 5 (3) or Article XIV, Sec. 1.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-402(16)(b): the amount of proceeds of sale of revenue bonds received by the state;

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-402(16)(d): the total amount of all fees and expenses relating to the issuance of the revenue bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-402(16)(e): the amount of sale proceeds of the revenue bonds used to pay fees and expenses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-402(16)(f): the amount of sale proceeds of the revenue bonds deposited in the reserve fund established with respect to the issue of revenue bonds, if any.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-501 Tax status -- Exemption.
---------------------------------------------------------
The revenue bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the revenue bonds, and any income from the bonds is not taxable in Utah for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601 Publication of resolution or notice -- Limitation on actions to contest legality.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1): The commission may either:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(a): publish once in a newspaper having general circulation in Utah any resolution adopted by it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b): in lieu of publishing the entire resolution, publish a notice of revenue bonds to be issued, titled as such, containing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b)(i): the purpose of the revenue bond issue;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b)(ii): the maximum principal amount that may be issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b)(iii): the maximum number of years over which the revenue bonds may mature;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b)(iv): the maximum interest rate that the revenue bonds may bear, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b)(v): the maximum discount from par, expressed as a percentage of principal amount, at which the revenue bonds may be sold; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(1)(b)(vi): a statement that a copy of the resolution or other bond document may be examined at the office of the state treasurer during regular business hours for at least 30 days after the publication of the notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(2): For 30 days after the date of publication, any interested person may contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(2)(a): the legality of the resolution or other bond document;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(2)(b): any of the revenue bonds authorized under it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(2)(c): any of the provisions made for the repayment of the revenue bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(3): After 30 days, a person may not, for any cause, contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(3)(a): the legality of the resolution or other bond document;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(3)(b): any of the revenue bonds authorized under the resolution or other bond document; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-601(3)(c): any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the revenue bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701 Payment of expenses.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701(1): 63B-1b-302; 63B-1b-402 All expenses incurred by the state under this chapter may be paid:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701(1)(a): 63B-1b-302 in the case of expenses incurred under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701(1)(b): 63B-1b-402 in the case of expenses incurred under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701(2)(a): Any expenses incurred by the state under this chapter that are not paid from the proceeds of the liquidation of agency bonds or the issuance of state revenue bonds shall be paid from the revolving funds of the authorizing agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-1b-701(2)(b): These expenses are not a charge to or an appropriation from the General Fund.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be used for the purposes described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-104 Manner of issuance -- Amounts, interest, and maturity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-104(1): Bonds issued under this chapter may be authorized, sold, and issued at times and in a manner determined by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-104(2): Bonds may be issued in one or more series, in amounts, and shall bear dates, interest rates, including a variable rate, and maturity dates as the commission determines by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-104(3): A bond issued may not mature later than 20 years after the date of final passage of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105 Terms and conditions of sale -- Plan of financing -- Signatures -- Replacement -- Registration -- Federal rebate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1): In the issuance of bonds, the commission may determine by resolution:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(a): the manner of sale, including public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(b): the terms and conditions of sale, including price, whether at, below, or above face value;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(c): denominations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(d): form;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(e): manner of execution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(f): manner of authentication;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(g): place and medium of purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(h): redemption terms; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(1)(i): other provisions and details it considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(2): The commission may by resolution adopt a plan of financing, which may include terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the commission on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for letters of credit, standby letters of credit, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements to secure the bonds, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(3)(a): Any signature of a public official authorized by resolution of the commission to sign the bonds may be a facsimile signature of that official imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(3)(b): If all signatures of public officials on the bonds are facsimile signatures, provision shall be made for a manual authenticating signature on the bonds by or on behalf of a designated authentication agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(3)(c): If an official ceases to hold office before delivery of the bonds signed by that official, the signature or facsimile signature of the official is nevertheless valid for all purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(3)(d): A facsimile of the state seal may be imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(4)(a): The commission may enact resolutions providing for the replacement of lost, destroyed, or mutilated bonds, or for the exchange of bonds after issuance for bonds of smaller or larger denominations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(4)(b): Bonds in changed denominations shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(4)(b)(i): be exchanged for the original bonds in like aggregate principal amounts and in a manner that prevents the duplication of interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(4)(b)(ii): bear interest at the same rate, mature on the same date, and be as nearly as practicable in the form of the original bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(5): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305; Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(5)(a): Bonds may be registered as to both principal and interest or may be in a book entry form under which the right to principal and interest may be transferred only through a book entry.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(5)(b): The commission may provide for the services and payment for the services of one or more financial institutions or other entities or persons, or nominees, within or outside the state, for the authentication, registration, transfer, including record, bookkeeping, or book entry functions, exchange, and payment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(5)(c): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305 The records of ownership, registration, transfer, and exchange of the bonds, and of persons to whom payment with respect to the obligations is made, are private records as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(5)(d): Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act The bonds and any evidences of participation interest in the bonds may be issued, executed, authenticated, registered, transferred, exchanged, and otherwise made to comply with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(6): The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(6)(a): by resolution, provide for payment to the United States of whatever amounts are necessary to comply with Section 148 (f) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(6)(b): enter into agreements with financial and other institutions and attorneys to provide for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(6)(b)(i): the calculation, holding, and payment of those amounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-105(6)(b)(ii): payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under any agreements entered into by the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-106 Constitutional debt limitation.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-106(1): The commission may not issue bonds under this chapter in an amount that violates the limitation described in Article XIV, Sec.  1, Utah Constitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-106(2): For purposes of applying the debt limitation contained in Article XIV, Sec.  1, Utah Constitution, the value of the taxable property in Utah is considered to be 100% of the fair market value of the taxable property of the state, as computed from the last assessment for state purposes previous to the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107 Tax levy -- Abatement of tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(1): Each year after issuance of the bonds and until all outstanding bonds are retired, there is levied a direct annual tax on all real and personal property within the state subject to state taxation, sufficient to pay:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(1)(a): applicable bond redemption premiums, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(1)(b): interest on the bonds as it becomes due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(1)(c): principal of the bonds as it becomes due.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(2)(a): The State Tax Commission shall fix the rate of the direct annual tax levy each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(2)(b): The tax shall be collected and the proceeds applied as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-107(3): The direct annual tax imposed under this section is abated to the extent money is available from sources, other than ad valorem taxes in the sinking fund, for the payment of bond interest, principal, and redemption premiums.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-108 Creation of sinking fund.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-108(1): There is created a sinking fund, to be administered by the state treasurer, entitled the "1993 General Obligation Bonds Sinking Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-108(2): All money deposited in the sinking fund, from whatever source, shall be used to pay debt service on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-108(3): The proceeds of all taxes levied under this chapter are appropriated to this fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-108(4): The state treasurer may create separate accounts within the sinking fund for each series of bonds issued.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-109 Payment of interest, principal, and redemption premiums.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-109(1): The Division of Finance shall draw warrants on the state treasury before any interest, principal, or redemption premiums become due on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-109(2): After receipt of the warrants, the state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-109(2)(a): promptly pay the warrants from funds within the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-109(2)(b): immediately transmit the amount paid to the paying agent for the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-110 Investment of sinking fund money.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-110(1): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-110(2): Unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter, the treasurer shall retain all income from the investment of any money contained in the sinking fund in the sinking fund and use it for the payment of debt service on the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111 Bond proceeds -- Deposits -- Investment -- Disposition of investment income and unexpended proceeds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(1)(a): Proceeds from the sale of bonds issued under this chapter shall be deposited within one or more accounts as determined by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(1)(b): The state treasurer shall administer and maintain these accounts unless otherwise provided by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(1)(c): The commission by resolution may provide for the deposit of the money with a trustee and the administration, disposition, or investment of the money by this trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(2)(a): The commission by resolution shall provide for the kinds of investments in which the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter may be invested.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(2)(b): Income from the investment of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be applied as provided by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-111(3): Any unexpended bond proceeds issued under this chapter shall be deposited, upon completion of the purposes for which the bonds were issued, in the sinking fund, unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-112(2): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act For purposes of


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-113 Certification of satisfaction of conditions precedent -- Conclusiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-113(1): The commission may not issue any bond under this chapter until it finds and certifies that all conditions precedent to issuance of the bonds have been satisfied.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-113(2): A recital on any bond of this finding and certification conclusively establishes the completion and satisfaction of all conditions precedent.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-114 Tax exemption.
----------------------------------------------
The bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the bonds, and any income from the bonds are not taxable in this state for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-115 Legal investment status.
--------------------------------------------------------
Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments for all state trust funds, insurance companies, banks, trust companies, and the State School Fund and may be used as collateral to secure legal obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116 Publication of resolution or notice -- Limitation on actions to contest legality.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(1): 45-1-101; 11-14-316(2) The commission may:

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(2)(a): Any interested person, for 30 days after the date of publication, may contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(2)(a)(i): the legality of the resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(2)(a)(ii): any of the bonds authorized under it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(2)(a)(iii): any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-116(2)(b): After 30 days, a person may not contest the legality of the resolution, any of the bonds authorized under it, or any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds for any cause.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-117 Report to Legislature.
------------------------------------------------------
The governor shall report the commission's proceedings to each annual general session of the Legislature in his budget for as long as bonds issued under this chapter remain outstanding.

---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-206(1): The commission may not issue bonds under this chapter in an amount that violates the limitation described in Article XIV, Sec.  1, Utah Constitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-206(2): For purposes of applying the debt limitation contained in Article XIV, Sec.  1, Utah Constitution, the value of the taxable property in Utah is considered to be 100% of the fair market value of the taxable property of the state, as computed from the last assessment for state purposes previous to the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207 Tax levy -- Abatement of tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(1): Each year after issuance of the bonds and until all outstanding bonds are retired, there is levied a direct annual tax on all real and personal property within the state subject to state taxation, sufficient to pay:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(1)(a): applicable bond redemption premiums, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(1)(b): interest on the bonds as it becomes due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(1)(c): principal of the bonds as it becomes due.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(2)(a): The State Tax Commission shall fix the rate of the direct annual tax levy each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(2)(b): The tax shall be collected and the proceeds applied as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-207(3): The direct annual tax imposed under this section is abated to the extent money is available from sources, other than ad valorem taxes in the sinking fund, for the payment of bond interest, principal, and redemption premiums.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-208 Creation of sinking fund.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-208(1): There is created a sinking fund, to be administered by the state treasurer, entitled the "1993 Highway General Obligation Bonds Sinking Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-208(2): All money deposited in the sinking fund, from whatever source, shall be used to pay debt service on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-208(3): The proceeds of all taxes levied under this chapter are appropriated to this fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-208(4): The state treasurer may create separate accounts within the sinking fund for each series of bonds issued.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-209 Payment of interest, principal, and redemption premiums.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-209(1): The Division of Finance shall draw warrants on the state treasury before any interest, principal, or redemption premiums become due on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-209(2): After receipt of the warrants, the state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-209(2)(a): promptly pay the warrants from funds within the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-209(2)(b): immediately transmit the amount paid to the paying agent for the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-210 Investment of sinking fund money.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-210(1): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-210(2): Unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter, the treasurer shall retain all income from the investment of any money contained in the sinking fund in the sinking fund and use it for the payment of debt service on the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211 Bond proceeds -- Deposits -- Investment -- Disposition of investment income and unexpended proceeds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(1)(a): Proceeds from the sale of bonds issued under this chapter shall be deposited within one or more accounts as determined by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(1)(b): The state treasurer shall administer and maintain these accounts unless otherwise provided by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(1)(c): The commission by resolution may provide for the deposit of the money with a trustee and the administration, disposition, or investment of the money by this trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(2)(a): The commission by resolution shall provide for the kinds of investments in which the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter may be invested.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(2)(b): Income from the investment of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be applied as provided by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-211(3): Any unexpended bond proceeds issued under this chapter shall be deposited, upon completion of the purposes for which the bonds were issued, in the sinking fund, unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-212 Refunding of bonds.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-212(1): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act The commission may provide for the refunding of any of the bonds in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-212(2): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act For purposes of


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-213 Certification of satisfaction of conditions precedent -- Conclusiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-213(1): The commission may not issue any bond under this chapter until it finds and certifies that all conditions precedent to issuance of the bonds have been satisfied.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-213(2): A recital on any bond of this finding and certification conclusively establishes the completion and satisfaction of all such conditions.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-214 Tax exemption.
----------------------------------------------
The bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the bonds, and any income from the bonds are not taxable in this state for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-215 Legal investment status.
--------------------------------------------------------
Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments for all state trust funds, insurance companies, banks, trust companies, and the State School Fund and may be used as collateral to secure legal obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216 Publication of resolution or notice -- Limitation on actions to contest legality.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(1): 45-1-101; 11-14-316(2) The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(1)(a): 45-1-101 publish any resolution it adopts under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(1)(a)(i): once in a newspaper having general circulation in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(1)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(1)(b): 11-14-316(2) in lieu of publishing the entire resolution, publish a notice of bonds to be issued, titled as such, containing the information required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(2)(a): Any interested person, for 30 days after the date of publication, may contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(2)(a)(i): the legality of the resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(2)(a)(ii): any of the bonds authorized under it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(2)(a)(iii): any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-216(2)(b): After 30 days, a person may not contest the legality of the resolution, any of the bonds authorized under it, or any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds for any cause.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-2-217 Report to Legislature.
------------------------------------------------------
The governor shall report the commission's proceedings to each annual general session of the Legislature in his budget for as long as bonds issued under this chapter remain outstanding.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102 Maximum amount -- Projects authorized.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(1): The total amount of bonds issued under this part may not exceed $64,600,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(a): Proceeds from the issuance of bonds shall be provided to the division to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of acquiring and constructing the projects listed in this Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(b): These costs may include the cost of acquiring land, interests in land, easements and rights-of-way, improving sites, and acquiring, constructing, equipping, and furnishing facilities and all structures, roads, parking facilities, utilities, and improvements necessary, incidental, or convenient to the facilities, interest estimated to accrue on these bonds during the period to be covered by construction of the projects plus a period of six months after the end of the construction period and all related engineering, architectural, and legal fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(c): For the division, proceeds shall be provided for the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(d): For purposes of this section, operations and maintenance costs:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(d)(i): are estimates only;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(d)(ii): may include any operations and maintenance costs already funded in existing agency budgets; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(2)(d)(iii): are not commitments by this Legislature or future Legislatures to fund those operations and maintenance costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(3)(a): The amounts funded as listed in Subsection (2) are estimates only and do not constitute a limitation on the amount that may be expended for any project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(3)(b): The board may revise these estimates and redistribute the amount estimated for a project among the projects authorized.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(3)(c): The commission, by resolution and in consultation with the board, may delete one or more projects from this list if the inclusion of that project or those projects in the list could be construed to violate state law or federal law or regulation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(4)(a): The division may enter into agreements related to these projects before the receipt of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(4)(b): The division shall make those expenditures from unexpended and unencumbered building funds already appropriated to the Capital Projects Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(4)(c): The division shall reimburse the Capital Projects Fund upon receipt of the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(4)(d): The commission may, by resolution, make any statement of intent relating to that reimbursement that is necessary or desirable to comply with federal tax law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(5)(a): For those projects for which only partial funding is provided in Subsection (2), it is the intent of the Legislature that the balance necessary to complete the projects be addressed by future Legislatures, either through appropriations or through the issuance or sale of bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(5)(b): For those phased projects, the division may enter into contracts for amounts not to exceed the anticipated full project funding but may not allow work to be performed on those contracts in excess of the funding already authorized by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(5)(c): Those contracts shall contain a provision for termination of the contract for the convenience of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-102(5)(d): It is also the intent of the Legislature that this authorization to the division does not bind future Legislatures to fund projects initiated from this authorization.
