Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-104 Manner of issuance -- Amounts, interest, and maturity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-104(1): Bonds issued under this chapter may be authorized, sold, and issued at times and in a manner determined by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-104(2): Bonds may be issued in one or more series, in amounts, and shall bear dates, interest rates, including a variable rate, and maturity dates as the commission determines by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-104(3): A bond issued may not mature later than 20 years after the date of final passage of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105 Terms and conditions of sale -- Plan of financing -- Signatures -- Replacement -- Registration -- Federal rebate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1): In the issuance of bonds, the commission may determine by resolution:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(a): the manner of sale, including public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(b): the terms and conditions of sale, including price, whether at, below, or above face value;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(c): denominations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(d): form;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(e): manner of execution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(f): manner of authentication;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(g): place and medium of purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(h): redemption terms; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(1)(i): other provisions and details it considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(2): The commission may by resolution adopt a plan of financing, which may include terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the commission on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for letters of credit, standby letters of credit, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements to secure the bonds, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(3)(a): Any signature of a public official authorized by resolution of the commission to sign the bonds may be a facsimile signature of that official imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(3)(b): If all signatures of public officials on the bonds are facsimile signatures, provision shall be made for a manual authenticating signature on the bonds by or on behalf of a designated authentication agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(3)(c): If an official ceases to hold office before delivery of the bonds signed by that official, the signature or facsimile signature of the official is nevertheless valid for all purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(3)(d): A facsimile of the state seal may be imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(4)(a): The commission may enact resolutions providing for the replacement of lost, destroyed, or mutilated bonds, or for the exchange of bonds after issuance for bonds of smaller or larger denominations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(4)(b): Bonds in changed denominations shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(4)(b)(i): be exchanged for the original bonds in like aggregate principal amounts and in a manner that prevents the duplication of interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(4)(b)(ii): bear interest at the same rate, mature on the same date, and be as nearly as practicable in the form of the original bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(5): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305; Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(5)(a): Bonds may be registered as to both principal and interest or may be in a book entry form under which the right to principal and interest may be transferred only through a book entry.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(5)(b): The commission may provide for the services and payment for the services of one or more financial institutions or other entities or persons, or nominees, within or outside the state, for the authentication, registration, transfer, including record, bookkeeping, or book entry functions, exchange, and payment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(5)(c): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305 The records of ownership, registration, transfer, and exchange of the bonds, and of persons to whom payment with respect to the obligations is made, are private records as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(5)(d): Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act The bonds and any evidences of participation interest in the bonds may be issued, executed, authenticated, registered, transferred, exchanged, and otherwise made to comply with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(6): The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(6)(a): by resolution, provide for payment to the United States of whatever amounts are necessary to comply with Section 148 (f) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-105(6)(b): enter into agreements with financial and other institutions and attorneys to provide for:

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-113 Certification of satisfaction of conditions precedent -- Conclusiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-113(1): The commission may not issue any bond under this chapter until it finds and certifies that all conditions precedent to issuance of the bonds have been satisfied.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-113(2): A recital on any bond of this finding and certification conclusively establishes the completion and satisfaction of all conditions precedent.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-114 Tax exemption.
----------------------------------------------
The bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the bonds, and any income from the bonds are not taxable in this state for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-115 Legal investment status.
--------------------------------------------------------
Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments for all state trust funds, insurance companies, banks, trust companies, and the State School Fund and may be used as collateral to secure legal obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116 Publication of resolution or notice -- Limitation on actions to contest legality.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(1): 45-1-101; 11-14-316(2) The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(1)(a): 45-1-101 publish any resolution it adopts under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(1)(a)(i): once in a newspaper having general circulation in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(1)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(1)(b): 11-14-316(2) in lieu of publishing the entire resolution, publish a notice of bonds to be issued, titled as such, containing the information required in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(2)(a): Any interested person, for 30 days after the date of publication, may contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(2)(a)(i): the legality of the resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(2)(a)(ii): any of the bonds authorized under it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(2)(a)(iii): any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-116(2)(b): After 30 days, a person may not contest the legality of the resolution, any of the bonds authorized under it, or any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds for any cause.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-117 Report to Legislature.
------------------------------------------------------
The governor shall report the commission's proceedings to each annual general session of the Legislature in his budget for as long as bonds issued under this chapter remain outstanding.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202 Maximum amount -- Projects authorized.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2):

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2)(a)(i): not more than $7,250,000 to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of constructing the Bangerter Highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2)(a)(ii): not more than $2,000,000 to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of enhancing and improving the 90th South interchange;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2)(a)(iii): not more than $1,000,000 to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of enhancing and improving the I-15 interchange at South University Avenue in Provo;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2)(a)(iv): not more than $250,000 to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of the Ogden I-15 Environmental Study; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2)(a)(v): not more than $1,500,000 to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of constructing class II sound walls on the interstate system in Salt Lake County according to the Department of Transportation priority list.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(2)(b): These costs may include the cost of acquiring land, interests in land, easements and rights-of-way, improving sites, and making all improvements necessary, incidental, or convenient to the facilities, interest estimated to accrue on these bonds during the period to be covered by construction of the projects plus a period of six months after the end of the construction period, and all related engineering, architectural, and legal fees.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(4): The commission may, by resolution, make any statement of intent relating to that reimbursement that is necessary or desirable to comply with federal tax law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-202(5): The Department of Transportation may enter into agreements related to that project before the receipt of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be used for the purposes described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-204 Manner of issuance -- Amounts, interest, and maturity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-204(1): Bonds issued under this chapter may be authorized, sold, and issued at times and in a manner determined by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-204(2): Bonds may be issued in one or more series, in amounts, and shall bear dates, interest rates, including a variable rate, and maturity dates as the commission determines by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-204(3): A bond issued may not mature later than 20 years after the date of final passage of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205 Terms and conditions of sale -- Plan of financing -- Signatures -- Replacement -- Registration -- Federal rebate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1): In the issuance of bonds, the commission may determine by resolution:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(a): the manner of sale, including public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(b): the terms and conditions of sale, including price, whether at, below, or above face value;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(c): denominations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(d): form;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(e): manner of execution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(f): manner of authentication;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(g): place and medium of purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(h): redemption terms; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(1)(i): other provisions and details it considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(2): The commission may by resolution adopt a plan of financing which may include terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the commission on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for letters of credit, standby letters of credit, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements to secure the bonds, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(3)(a): Any signature of a public official authorized by resolution of the commission to sign the bonds may be a facsimile signature of that official imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(3)(b): If all signatures of public officials on the bonds are facsimile signatures, provision shall be made for a manual authenticating signature on the bonds by or on behalf of a designated authentication agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(3)(c): If an official ceases to hold office before delivery of the bonds signed by that official, the signature or facsimile signature of the official is nevertheless valid for all purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(3)(d): A facsimile of the state seal may be imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(4)(a): The commission may enact resolutions providing for the replacement of lost, destroyed, or mutilated bonds, or for the exchange of bonds after issuance for bonds of smaller or larger denominations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(4)(b): Bonds in changed denominations shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(4)(b)(i): be exchanged for the original bonds in like aggregate principal amounts and in a manner that prevents the duplication of interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(4)(b)(ii): bear interest at the same rate, mature on the same date, and be as nearly as practicable in the form of the original bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(5): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305; Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(5)(a): Bonds may be registered as to both principal and interest or may be in a book entry form under which the right to principal and interest may be transferred only through a book entry.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(5)(b): The commission may provide for the services and payment for the services of one or more financial institutions or other entities or persons, or nominees, within or outside the state, for the authentication, registration, transfer, including record, bookkeeping, or book entry functions, exchange, and payment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(5)(c): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305 The records of ownership, registration, transfer, and exchange of the bonds, and of persons to whom payment with respect to the obligations is made, are private records as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(5)(d): Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act The bonds and any evidences of participation interest in the bonds may be issued, executed, authenticated, registered, transferred, exchanged, and otherwise made to comply with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(6): The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(6)(a): by resolution, provide for payment to the United States of whatever amounts are necessary to comply with Section 148 (f) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(6)(b): enter into agreements with financial and other institutions and attorneys to provide for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(6)(b)(i): the calculation, holding, and payment of those amounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-205(6)(b)(ii): payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under any agreements entered into by the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-206 Constitutional debt limitation.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-206(1): The commission may not issue bonds under this chapter in an amount that violates the limitation described in Article XIV, Sec. 1, Utah Constitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-206(2): For purposes of applying the debt limitation contained in Article XIV, Sec. 1, Utah Constitution, the value of the taxable property in Utah is considered to be 100% of the fair market value of the taxable property of the state, as computed from the last assessment for state purposes previous to the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207 Tax levy -- Abatement of tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(1): Each year after issuance of the bonds and until all outstanding bonds are retired, there is levied a direct annual tax on all real and personal property within the state subject to state taxation, sufficient to pay:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(1)(a): applicable bond redemption premiums, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(1)(b): interest on the bonds as it becomes due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(1)(c): principal of the bonds as it becomes due.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(2)(a): The State Tax Commission shall fix the rate of the direct annual tax levy each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(2)(b): The tax shall be collected and the proceeds applied as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-207(3): The direct annual tax imposed under this section is abated to the extent money is available from sources, other than ad valorem taxes in the sinking fund, for the payment of bond interest, principal, and redemption premiums.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-208 Creation of sinking fund.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-208(1): There is created a sinking fund, to be administered by the state treasurer, entitled the "1994 Highway General Obligation Bonds Sinking Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-208(2): All money deposited in the sinking fund, from whatever source, shall be used to pay debt service on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-208(3): The proceeds of all taxes levied under this chapter are appropriated to this fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-208(4): The state treasurer may create separate accounts within the sinking fund for each series of bonds issued.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-209 Payment of interest, principal, and redemption premiums.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-209(1): The Division of Finance shall draw warrants on the state treasury before any interest, principal, or redemption premiums become due on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-209(2): After receipt of the warrants, the state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-209(2)(a): promptly pay the warrants from funds within the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-209(2)(b): immediately transmit the amount paid to the paying agent for the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-210 Investment of sinking fund money.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-210(1): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-210(2): Unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter, the treasurer shall retain all income from the investment of any money contained in the sinking fund in the sinking fund and use it for the payment of debt service on the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211 Bond proceeds -- Deposits -- Investment -- Disposition of investment income and unexpended proceeds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(1)(a): Proceeds from the sale of bonds issued under this chapter shall be deposited within one or more accounts as determined by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(1)(b): The state treasurer shall administer and maintain these accounts unless otherwise provided by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(1)(c): The commission by resolution may provide for the deposit of the money with a trustee and the administration, disposition, or investment of the money by this trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(2)(a): The commission by resolution shall provide for the kinds of investments in which the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter may be invested.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(2)(b): Income from the investment of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be applied as provided by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-211(3): Any unexpended bond proceeds issued under this chapter shall be deposited, upon completion of the purposes for which the bonds were issued, in the sinking fund, unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301 Legislative intent -- Additional projects.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(1): It is the intent of the Legislature that, for any lease purchase agreement that the Legislature may authorize the Division of Facilities Construction and Management to enter into during its 1994 Annual General Session, the State Building Ownership Authority, at the reasonable rates and amounts it may determine, and with technical assistance from the state treasurer, the director of the Division of Finance, and the executive director of the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget, may seek out the most cost effective and prudent lease purchase plans available to the state and may, pursuant to Chapter 1, Part 3, State Building Ownership Authority Act, certificate out interests in, or obligations of the authority pertaining to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(1)(a): the lease purchase obligation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(1)(b): lease rental payments under the lease purchase obligation.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(3): It is the intent of the Legislature that the Division of Facilities Construction and Management allocate funds from the Capital Improvement appropriation and donations to cover costs associated with the upgrade of the Governor's Residence that go beyond the restoration costs which can be covered by insurance proceeds.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(9): If S.B. 275, 1994 General Session, which authorizes funding for a Courts Complex in Salt Lake City, becomes law, it is the intent of the Legislature that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(9)(a): the Legislative Management Committee, the Interim Appropriation Subcommittees for General Government and Capital Facilities and Executive Offices, Courts, and Corrections, the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst, the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget, and the Division of Facilities Construction and Management participate in a review of the proposed facility design for the Courts Complex no later than December 1994; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(9)(b): although this review will not affect the funding authorization issued by the 1994 Legislature, it is expected that Division of Facilities Construction and Management will give proper attention to concerns raised in these reviews and make appropriate design changes pursuant to the review.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10): It is the intent of the Legislature that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(a): the Division of Facilities Construction and Management, in cooperation with the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services, formerly known as the Division of Youth Corrections and then the Division of Juvenile Justice Services, develop a flexible use prototype facility for the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(b): the development process use existing prototype proposals unless it can be quantifiably demonstrated that the proposals cannot be used;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(c): the facility is designed so that with minor modifications, it can accommodate detention, observation and assessment, transition, and secure programs as needed at specific geographical locations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(d)(i): funding as provided in the fiscal year 1995 bond authorization for the Division of Youth Corrections , now known as the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services, is used to design and construct one facility and design the other;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(d)(ii): the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(d)(ii)(A): determine the location for the facility for which design and construction are fully funded; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(d)(ii)(B): in conjunction with the Division of Facilities Construction and Management, determine the best methodology for design and construction of the fully funded facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(e): the Division of Facilities Construction and Management submit the prototype as soon as possible to the Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee and Executive Offices, Criminal Justice, and Legislature Appropriation Subcommittee for review;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(f): the Division of Facilities Construction and Management issue a Request for Proposal for one of the facilities, with that facility designed and constructed entirely by the winning firm;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(g): the other facility be designed and constructed under the existing Division of Facilities Construction and Management process;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(h): both facilities follow the program needs and specifications as identified by Division of Facilities Construction and Management and the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services in the prototype; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(10)(i): the fully funded facility should be ready for occupancy by September 1, 1995.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(11): It is the intent of the Legislature that the fiscal year 1995 funding for the State Fair Park Master Study be used by the Division of Facilities Construction and Management to develop a master plan for the State Fair Park that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(11)(a): identifies capital facilities needs, capital improvement needs, building configuration, and other long term needs and uses of the State Fair Park and its buildings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(11)(b): establishes priorities for development, estimated costs, and projected timetables.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12): It is the intent of the Legislature that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12)(a): the Division of Facilities Construction and Management, in cooperation with the Division of State Parks, formerly known as the Division of Parks and Recreation, and surrounding counties, develop a master plan and general program for the phased development of Antelope Island;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12)(b): the master plan:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12)(b)(i): establish priorities for development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12)(b)(ii): include estimated costs and projected time tables; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12)(b)(iii): include recommendations for funding methods and the allocation of responsibilities between the parties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(12)(c): the results of the effort be reported to the Natural Resources, Agriculture, and Environmental Quality Appropriations Subcommittee and Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(13): It is the intent of the Legislature to authorize the University of Utah to use:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(13)(a): bond reserves to plan, design, and construct the Kingsbury Hall renovation under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(13)(b): donated and other nonappropriated funds to plan, design, and construct the Biology Research Building under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(14): It is the intent of the Legislature to authorize Utah State University to use:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(14)(a): federal and other funds to plan, design, and construct the Bee Lab under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(14)(b): donated and other nonappropriated funds to plan, design, and construct an Athletic Facility addition and renovation under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(14)(c): donated and other nonappropriated funds to plan, design, and construct a renovation to the Nutrition and Food Science Building under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(14)(d): federal and private funds to plan, design, and construct the Millville Research Facility under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(15): It is the intent of the Legislature to authorize Salt Lake Community College to use:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(15)(a): institutional funds to plan, design, and construct a remodel to the Auto Trades Office and Learning Center under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(15)(b): institutional funds to plan, design, and construct the relocation and expansion of a temporary maintenance compound under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(15)(c): institutional funds to plan, design, and construct the Alder Amphitheater under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(16): It is the intent of the Legislature to authorize Southern Utah University to use:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(16)(a): federal funds to plan, design, and construct a Community Services Building under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(16)(b): donated and other nonappropriated funds to plan, design, and construct a stadium expansion under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(17): It is the intent of the Legislature to authorize the Department of Corrections to use donated funds to plan, design, and construct a Prison Chapel at the Central Utah Correctional Facility in Gunnison under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(18): If the Utah National Guard does not relocate in the Signetics Building, it is the intent of the Legislature to authorize the Guard to use federal funds and funds from Provo City to plan and design an Armory in Provo, Utah, under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(19): It is the intent of the Legislature that the Utah Department of Transportation use $250,000 of the fiscal year 1995 highway appropriation to fund an environmental study in Ogden, Utah of the 2600 North Corridor between Washington Boulevard and I-15.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(20): It is the intent of the Legislature that the Ogden-Weber Applied Technology Center use the money appropriated for fiscal year 1995 to design the Metal Trades Building and purchase equipment for use in that building that could be used in metal trades or other programs in other Applied Technology Centers.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(21): It is the intent of the Legislature that the Bridgerland Applied Technology Center and the Ogden-Weber Applied Technology Center projects as designed in fiscal year 1995 be considered as the highest priority projects for construction funding in fiscal year 1996.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22): It is the intent of the Legislature that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(a): the Division of Facilities Construction and Management complete physical space utilization standards by June 30, 1995, for the use of technology education activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(b): these standards are to be developed with and approved by the State Board of Education, the Board of Regents, and the Division of Facilities Construction and Management;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(c): these physical standards be used as the basis for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(c)(i): determining utilization of any technology space based on number of stations capable and occupied for any given hour of operation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(c)(ii): requests for any new space or remodeling;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(d): the fiscal year 1995 projects at the Bridgerland Applied Technology Center and the Ogden-Weber Applied Technology Center are exempt from this process; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(22)(e): the design of the Davis Applied Technology Center take into account the utilization formulas established by the Division of Facilities Construction and Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(23): It is the intent of the Legislature that Utah Valley State College may use the money from the bond allocated to the remodel of the Signetics building to relocate its technical education programs at other designated sites or facilities under the supervision of the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management unless supervisory authority is delegated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(24): It is the intent of the Legislature that the money provided for the fiscal year 1995 project for the Bridgerland Applied Technology Center be used to design and construct the space associated with Utah State University and design the technology center portion of the project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-3-301(25): It is the intent of the Legislature that the governor provide periodic reports on the expenditure of the funds provided for electronic technology, equipment, and hardware to the Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee, and the Legislative Management Committee.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-101 State Bonding Commission authorized to issue general obligation bonds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The commission created under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102 Maximum amount -- Projects authorized.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
PROJECTUtah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(1): The total amount of bonds issued under this part may not exceed $45,300,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(a): Proceeds from the issuance of bonds shall be provided to the division to provide funds to pay all or part of the cost of acquiring and constructing the projects listed in this Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(b): These costs may include the cost of acquiring land, interests in land, easements and rights-of-way, improving sites, and acquiring, constructing, equipping, and furnishing facilities and all structures, roads, parking facilities, utilities, and improvements necessary, incidental, or convenient to the facilities, interest estimated to accrue on these bonds during the period to be covered by construction of the projects plus a period of six months after the end of the construction period, and all related engineering, architectural, and legal fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(c): For the division, proceeds shall be provided for the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(d): For purposes of this section, operations and maintenance costs:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(d)(i): are estimates only;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(d)(ii): may include any operations and maintenance costs already funded in existing agency budgets; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(2)(d)(iii): are not commitments by this Legislature or future Legislatures to fund those operations and maintenance costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(3)(a): The amounts funded as listed in Subsection (2) are estimates only and do not constitute a limitation on the amount that may be expended for any project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(3)(b): The board may revise these estimates and redistribute the amount estimated for a project among the projects authorized.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(3)(c): The commission, by resolution and in consultation with the board, may delete one or more projects from this list if the inclusion of that project or those projects in the list could be construed to violate state law or federal law or regulation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(4)(a): The division may enter into agreements related to these projects before the receipt of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(4)(b): The division shall make those expenditures from unexpended and unencumbered building funds already appropriated to the Capital Projects Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(4)(c): The division shall reimburse the Capital Projects Fund upon receipt of the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(4)(d): The commission may, by resolution, make any statement of intent relating to that reimbursement that is necessary or desirable to comply with federal tax law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(5)(a): For those projects for which only partial funding is provided in Subsection (2), it is the intent of the Legislature that the balance necessary to complete the projects be addressed by future Legislatures, either through appropriations or through the issuance or sale of bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(5)(b): For those phased projects, the division may enter into contracts for amounts not to exceed the anticipated full project funding but may not allow work to be performed on those contracts in excess of the funding already authorized by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(5)(c): Those contracts shall contain a provision for termination of the contract for the convenience of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-102(5)(d): It is also the intent of the Legislature that this authorization to the division does not bind future Legislatures to fund projects initiated from this authorization.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-103 Use of bond proceeds for issuance and other costs.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be used for the purposes described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-104 Manner of issuance -- Amounts, interest, and maturity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-104(1): Bonds issued under this chapter may be authorized, sold, and issued at times and in a manner determined by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-104(2): Bonds may be issued in one or more series, in amounts, and shall bear dates, interest rates, including a variable rate, and maturity dates as the commission determines by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-104(3): A bond issued may not mature later than 20 years after the date of final passage of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105 Terms and conditions of sale -- Plan of financing -- Signatures -- Replacement -- Registration -- Federal rebate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1): In the issuance of bonds, the commission may determine by resolution:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(a): the manner of sale, including public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(b): the terms and conditions of sale, including price, whether at, below, or above face value;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(c): denominations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(d): form;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(e): manner of execution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(f): manner of authentication;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(g): place and medium of purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(h): redemption terms; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(1)(i): other provisions and details it considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(2): The commission may by resolution adopt a plan of financing, which may include terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the commission on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for letters of credit, standby letters of credit, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements to secure the bonds, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(3)(a): Any signature of a public official authorized by resolution of the commission to sign the bonds may be a facsimile signature of that official imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(3)(b): If all signatures of public officials on the bonds are facsimile signatures, provision shall be made for a manual authenticating signature on the bonds by or on behalf of a designated authentication agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(3)(c): If an official ceases to hold office before delivery of the bonds signed by that official, the signature or facsimile signature of the official is nevertheless valid for all purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(3)(d): A facsimile of the state seal may be imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(4)(a): The commission may enact resolutions providing for the replacement of lost, destroyed, or mutilated bonds, or for the exchange of bonds after issuance for bonds of smaller or larger denominations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(4)(b): Bonds in changed denominations shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(4)(b)(i): be exchanged for the original bonds in like aggregate principal amounts and in a manner that prevents the duplication of interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(4)(b)(ii): bear interest at the same rate, mature on the same date, and be as nearly as practicable in the form of the original bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(5): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305; Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(5)(a): Bonds may be registered as to both principal and interest or may be in a book entry form under which the right to principal and interest may be transferred only through a book entry.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(5)(b): The commission may provide for the services and payment for the services of one or more financial institutions or other entities or persons, or nominees, within or outside the state, for the authentication, registration, transfer, including record, bookkeeping, or book entry functions, exchange, and payment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(5)(c): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305 The records of ownership, registration, transfer, and exchange of the bonds, and of persons to whom payment with respect to the obligations is made, are private records as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(5)(d): Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act The bonds and any evidences of participation interest in the bonds may be issued, executed, authenticated, registered, transferred, exchanged, and otherwise made to comply with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(6): The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(6)(a): by resolution, provide for payment to the United States of whatever amounts are necessary to comply with Section 148 (f) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(6)(b): enter into agreements with financial and other institutions and attorneys to provide for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(6)(b)(i): the calculation, holding, and payment of those amounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-105(6)(b)(ii): payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under any agreements entered into by the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-106 Constitutional debt limitation.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-106(1): The commission may not issue bonds under this chapter in an amount that violates the limitation described in Article XIV, Section 1, Utah Constitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-106(2): For purposes of applying the debt limitation contained in Article XIV, Section 1, Utah Constitution, the value of the taxable property in Utah is considered to be 100% of the fair market value of the taxable property of the state, as computed from the last assessment for state purposes previous to the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107 Tax levy -- Abatement of tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(1): Each year after issuance of the bonds and until all outstanding bonds are retired, there is levied a direct annual tax on all real and personal property within the state subject to state taxation, sufficient to pay:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(1)(a): applicable bond redemption premiums, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(1)(b): interest on the bonds as it becomes due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(1)(c): principal of the bonds as it becomes due.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(2)(a): The State Tax Commission shall fix the rate of the direct annual tax levy each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(2)(b): The tax shall be collected and the proceeds applied as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-107(3): The direct annual tax imposed under this section is abated to the extent money is available from sources, other than ad valorem taxes in the sinking fund, for the payment of bond interest, principal, and redemption premiums.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-108 Creation of sinking fund.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-108(1): There is created a sinking fund, to be administered by the state treasurer, entitled the "1995 General Obligation Bonds Sinking Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-108(2): All money deposited in the sinking fund, from whatever source, shall be used to pay debt service on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-108(3): The proceeds of all taxes levied under this chapter are appropriated to this fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-108(4): The state treasurer may create separate accounts within the sinking fund for each series of bonds issued.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-109 Payment of interest, principal, and redemption premiums.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-109(1): The Division of Finance shall draw warrants on the state treasury before any interest, principal, or redemption premiums become due on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-109(2): After receipt of the warrants, the state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-109(2)(a): promptly pay the warrants from funds within the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-109(2)(b): immediately transmit the amount paid to the paying agent for the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-110 Investment of sinking fund money.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-110(1): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-110(2): Unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter, the treasurer shall retain all income from the investment of any money contained in the sinking fund in the sinking fund and use it for the payment of debt service on the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111 Bond proceeds -- Deposits -- Investment -- Disposition of investment income and unexpended proceeds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(1)(a): Proceeds from the sale of bonds issued under this chapter shall be deposited within one or more accounts as determined by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(1)(b): The state treasurer shall administer and maintain these accounts unless otherwise provided by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(1)(c): The commission by resolution may provide for the deposit of the money with a trustee and the administration, disposition, or investment of the money by this trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(2)(a): The commission by resolution shall provide for the kinds of investments in which the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter may be invested.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(2)(b): Income from the investment of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be applied as provided by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-111(3): Any unexpended bond proceeds issued under this chapter shall be deposited, upon completion of the purposes for which the bonds were issued, in the sinking fund, unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-112 Refunding of bonds.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-112(1): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act The commission may provide for the refunding of any of the bonds in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-112(2): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act For purposes of


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-113 Certification of satisfaction of conditions precedent -- Conclusiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-113(1): The commission may not issue any bond under this chapter until it finds and certifies that all conditions precedent to issuance of the bonds have been satisfied.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-113(2): A recital on any bond of this finding and certification conclusively establishes the completion and satisfaction of all conditions precedent.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-114 Tax exemption.
----------------------------------------------
The bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the bonds, and any income from the bonds are not taxable in this state for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-115 Legal investment status.
--------------------------------------------------------
Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments for all state trust funds, insurance companies, banks, trust companies, and the State School Fund and may be used as collateral to secure legal obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116 Publication of resolution or notice -- Limitation on actions to contest legality.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(1): 45-1-101; 11-14-316(2) The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(1)(a): 45-1-101 publish any resolution it adopts under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(1)(a)(i): once in a newspaper having general circulation in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(1)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(1)(b): 11-14-316(2) in lieu of publishing the entire resolution, publish a notice of bonds to be issued, titled as such, containing the information required in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(2)(a): Any interested person, for 30 days after the date of publication, may contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(2)(a)(i): the legality of the resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(2)(a)(ii): any of the bonds authorized under it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(2)(a)(iii): any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-116(2)(b): After 30 days, a person may not contest the legality of the resolution, any of the bonds authorized under it, or any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds for any cause.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-4-117 Report to Legislature.
------------------------------------------------------
The governor shall report the commission's proceedings to each annual general session of the Legislature in his budget for as long as bonds issued under this chapter remain outstanding.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-103 Use of bond proceeds for issuance and other costs.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be used for the purposes described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-104 Manner of issuance -- Amounts, interest, and maturity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-104(1): Bonds issued under this chapter may be authorized, sold, and issued at times and in a manner determined by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-104(2): Bonds may be issued in one or more series, in amounts, and shall bear dates, interest rates, including a variable rate, and maturity dates as the commission determines by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-104(3): A bond issued may not mature later than 20 years after the date of final passage of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105 Terms and conditions of sale -- Plan of financing -- Signatures -- Replacement -- Registration -- Federal rebate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1): In the issuance of bonds, the commission may determine by resolution:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(a): the manner of sale, including public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(b): the terms and conditions of sale, including price, whether at, below, or above face value;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(c): denominations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(d): form;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(e): manner of execution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(f): manner of authentication;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(g): place and medium of purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(h): redemption terms; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(1)(i): other provisions and details it considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(2): The commission may by resolution adopt a plan of financing, which may include terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the commission on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for letters of credit, standby letters of credit, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements to secure the bonds, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(3)(a): Any signature of a public official authorized by resolution of the commission to sign the bonds may be a facsimile signature of that official imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(3)(b): If all signatures of public officials on the bonds are facsimile signatures, provision shall be made for a manual authenticating signature on the bonds by or on behalf of a designated authentication agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(3)(c): If an official ceases to hold office before delivery of the bonds signed by that official, the signature or facsimile signature of the official is nevertheless valid for all purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(3)(d): A facsimile of the state seal may be imprinted, engraved, stamped, or otherwise placed on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(4)(a): The commission may enact resolutions providing for the replacement of lost, destroyed, or mutilated bonds, or for the exchange of bonds after issuance for bonds of smaller or larger denominations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(4)(b): Bonds in changed denominations shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(4)(b)(i): be exchanged for the original bonds in like aggregate principal amounts and in a manner that prevents the duplication of interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(4)(b)(ii): bear interest at the same rate, mature on the same date, and be as nearly as practicable in the form of the original bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(5): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305; Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(5)(a): Bonds may be registered as to both principal and interest or may be in a book entry form under which the right to principal and interest may be transferred only through a book entry.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(5)(b): The commission may provide for the services and payment for the services of one or more financial institutions or other entities or persons, or nominees, within or outside the state, for the authentication, registration, transfer, including record, bookkeeping, or book entry functions, exchange, and payment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(5)(c): 63G-2-302; 63G-2-305 The records of ownership, registration, transfer, and exchange of the bonds, and of persons to whom payment with respect to the obligations are made, are private records as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(5)(d): Title 15, Chapter 7, Registered Public Obligations Act The bonds and any evidences of participation interest in the bonds may be issued, executed, authenticated, registered, transferred, exchanged, and otherwise made to comply with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(6): The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(6)(a): by resolution, provide for payment to the United States of whatever amounts are necessary to comply with Section 148 (f) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(6)(b): enter into agreements with financial and other institutions and attorneys to provide for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(6)(b)(i): the calculation, holding, and payment of those amounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-105(6)(b)(ii): payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under any agreements entered into by the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-106 Constitutional debt limitation.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-106(1): The commission may not issue bonds under this chapter in an amount that violates the limitation described in Utah Constitution Article XIV, Section 1.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-106(2): For purposes of applying the debt limitation contained in Utah Constitution Article XIV, Section 1, the value of the taxable property in Utah is considered to be 100% of the fair market value of the taxable property of the state, as computed from the last assessment for state purposes previous to the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107 Tax levy -- Abatement of tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(1): Each year after issuance of the bonds and until all outstanding bonds are retired, there is levied a direct annual tax on all real and personal property within the state subject to state taxation, sufficient to pay:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(1)(a): applicable bond redemption premiums, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(1)(b): interest on the bonds as it becomes due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(1)(c): principal of the bonds as it becomes due.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(2)(a): The State Tax Commission shall fix the rate of the direct annual tax levy each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(2)(b): The tax shall be collected and the proceeds applied as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-107(3): The direct annual tax imposed under this section is abated to the extent money is available from sources, other than ad valorem taxes in the sinking fund, for the payment of bond interest, principal, and redemption premiums.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-108 Creation of sinking fund.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-108(1): There is created a sinking fund, to be administered by the state treasurer, entitled the "1996 General Obligation Bonds Sinking Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-108(2): All money deposited in the sinking fund, from whatever source, shall be used to pay debt service on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-108(3): The proceeds of all taxes levied under this chapter are appropriated to this fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-108(4): The state treasurer may create separate accounts within the sinking fund for each series of bonds issued.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-109 Payment of interest, principal, and redemption premiums.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-109(1): The Division of Finance shall draw warrants on the state treasury before any interest, principal, or redemption premiums become due on the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-109(2): After receipt of the warrants, the state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-109(2)(a): promptly pay the warrants from funds within the sinking fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-109(2)(b): immediately transmit the amount paid to the paying agent for the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-110 Investment of sinking fund money.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-110(1): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-110(2): Unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter, the treasurer shall retain all income from the investment of any money contained in the sinking fund in the sinking fund and use it for the payment of debt service on the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111 Bond proceeds -- Deposits -- Investment -- Disposition of investment income and unexpended proceeds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(1)(a): Proceeds from the sale of bonds issued under this chapter shall be deposited within one or more accounts as determined by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(1)(b): The state treasurer shall administer and maintain these accounts unless otherwise provided by the commission by resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(1)(c): The commission by resolution may provide for the deposit of the money with a trustee and the administration, disposition, or investment of the money by this trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(2)(a): The commission by resolution shall provide for the kinds of investments in which the proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter may be invested.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(2)(b): Income from the investment of proceeds of bonds issued under this chapter shall be applied as provided by resolution of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-111(3): Any unexpended bond proceeds issued under this chapter shall be deposited, upon completion of the purposes for which the bonds were issued, in the sinking fund, unless otherwise provided in the resolution of the commission authorizing the issuance of bonds under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-112 Refunding of bonds.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-112(1): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act The commission may provide for the refunding of any of the bonds in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-112(2): Title 11, Chapter 27, Utah Refunding Bond Act For purposes of


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-113 Certification of satisfaction of conditions precedent -- Conclusiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-113(1): The commission may not issue any bond under this chapter until it finds and certifies that all conditions precedent to issuance of the bonds have been satisfied.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-113(2): A recital on any bond of this finding and certification conclusively establishes the completion and satisfaction of all conditions precedent.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-114 Tax exemption.
----------------------------------------------
The bonds issued under this chapter, any interest paid on the bonds, and any income from the bonds are not taxable in this state for any purpose, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-115 Legal investment status.
--------------------------------------------------------
Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments for all state trust funds, insurance companies, banks, trust companies, and the State School Fund and may be used as collateral to secure legal obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116 Publication of resolution or notice -- Limitation on actions to contest legality.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(1): 45-1-101; 11-14-316(2) The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(1)(a): 45-1-101 publish any resolution it adopts under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(1)(a)(i): once in a newspaper having general circulation in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(1)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(1)(b): 11-14-316(2) in lieu of publishing the entire resolution, publish a notice of bonds to be issued, titled as such, containing the information required in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(2)(a): Any interested person, for 30 days after the date of publication, may contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(2)(a)(i): the legality of the resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(2)(a)(ii): any of the bonds authorized under it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(2)(a)(iii): any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-116(2)(b): After 30 days, a person may not contest the legality of the resolution, any of the bonds authorized under it, or any of the provisions made for the security and repayment of the bonds for any cause.


Utah Code Annotated § 63B-5-117 Report to Legislature.
------------------------------------------------------
The governor shall report the commission's proceedings to each annual general session of the Legislature in his budget for as long as bonds issued under this chapter remain outstanding.
